<div id="review_139909236" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139909236" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3820960-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553552424p2/3820960.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139909236?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/3820960-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/11372739-wolfsbane">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3820960-jess?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3820960-jess?shelf=ruined-series">ruined-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139909236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10783542461796294112"><b>"This is only about love."</b><br/><br/><br/>This was totally worth the wait :D <br/><br/>I was so excited when I finally received this to review (bit late but better late than never). I'll try and give this the review it deserves. <br/><br/>I loved it more than I thought I would! Andrea Cremer totally outdid herself in this book. Everything was really fast paced and just intense that I was on the edge of my seat when I was reading it. All the questions that were raised about The Keepers in the first book are answered in this one, an</span>
  <span id="freeText10783542461796294112" style="display:none"><b>"This is only about love."</b><br /><br /><br />This was totally worth the wait :D <br /><br />I was so excited when I finally received this to review (bit late but better late than never). I'll try and give this the review it deserves. <br /><br />I loved it more than I thought I would! Andrea Cremer totally outdid herself in this book. Everything was really fast paced and just intense that I was on the edge of my seat when I was reading it. All the questions that were raised about The Keepers in the first book are answered in this one, and I loved seeing old enemies become new allies for Calla and her pack. <br /><br />I loved coming back to Calla and some of the older characters from the first book. When I read Nightshade I got so emotionally invested in all of them that I was so pleased to feel reunited with them all. New characters like Monroe, Connor (LOVE CONNORRR!!)Adne, and Ethan (love Ethan too), such fantastic new characters that brought some new life to some interesting moments to an already fabulous book. <br /><br />Now, as some of you are aware I'm team Ren, always was and always will be. The only gripe I have is that there just wasn't enough Ren, except for flashbacks and a couple of pages Ren wasn't around much. Which made me sad, I want more Ren. However having said that, I now understand why Andrea Cremer wrote Ren out of Wolfsbane because its the ending to this book that makes you understand and hope that Bloodrose will consist of Ren's story and the turn of events between himself, Calla and the Keepers lies. That's all I'm saying on the Ren subject, because I have a tendency to get carried away when I speak about Ren.<br /><br />Calla and Shay's relationship is tested but ultimately Calla's love for him gives her strength and allows her to make the decision that leads to the end of Wolfsbane.<br /><br />I honestly cannot wait for Bloodrose, to see more Ren, more Calla, Connor and Adne and I CANNOT wait to see how things with Sabine and Ethan turn out, THAT is going to be exciting stuff.<br /><br />Anyway, I read this whilst I was on holiday and I read it in about 3 days on the beach, it was a fantastic read and I'm so glad I read it. <br /><br />I can't wait to read Bloodrose and finally get everything tied up and answered! :)<br /><br />Read it guys, its fantastic <br /></span>

<div id="review_446824567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/446824567" />
    <a title="Chanzie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14188051-chanzie"><img alt="Chanzie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516420945p2/14188051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/446824567?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chanzie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chanzie" href="/user/show/14188051-chanzie">Chanzie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14188051-chanzie?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14188051-chanzie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14188051-chanzie?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer446824567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5597098494038940114">Wolfsbane picks up directly where Nightshade ended. The story is split into 3 parts in this book, and starts off with Calla and Shay adjusting to the searchers and forming new relationships. It has a lot of history and facts - It can come across as a small info dump but I found it fascinating. Initially I was worried that this was going to be a slow middle type book, but I was so wrong, and got completely caught up in Calla's world. <br/><br/>Characters & Story line: 5/5<br/><br/>Calla - This is such an intense jou</span>
  <span id="freeText5597098494038940114" style="display:none">Wolfsbane picks up directly where Nightshade ended. The story is split into 3 parts in this book, and starts off with Calla and Shay adjusting to the searchers and forming new relationships. It has a lot of history and facts - It can come across as a small info dump but I found it fascinating. Initially I was worried that this was going to be a slow middle type book, but I was so wrong, and got completely caught up in Calla's world. <br /><br />Characters &amp; Story line: 5/5<br /><br />Calla - This is such an intense journey for Calla. I related easily to her and found I actually loved her quite a lot more in Wolfsbane, than I did in Nightshade. Maybe it's because she considers Ren a little bit more and her heart aches for him in a different way. *tee hee* #TeamRen<br /><br />Shay - I liked him more in this book too. He is great with, and for, Calla. (Even though I am still Team Ren!). Shay is on the back burner a bit for me in Wolfsbane but we find out a lot about the role he plays and his past in this book. Shay is a great character, and I think his role in Bloodrose is going to be intense.<br /><br />Ren - Ren barely made an appearance in this book. I am still totally team Ren and really hope to see more of him in Bloodrose. <br /><br />Ansel - When Ansel first appeared my heart broke! He is a shadow of his former bubbly self and I really hope things change for him. <br /><br />Searchers - I enjoyed getting to know this group and really like Adne, Connor and Monroe.<br /><br />Plot, Pace, Writing style: 5/5 <br /><br /><br />Part 2 is where it really kicked up a gear for me. It is filled with love, friendship and heartbreak. This is a fast paced, exciting and intense read. It does end with quite a huge cliffhanger, and I am extremely glad that I have the next book so that I can continue the story without a break! My heart was left beating with intensity in my chest the way things ended with Calla, Shay, Ren and Adne. Wolfsbane is a middle type book but it is gearing up for an intense war in Bloodrose. <br /><br />Cover talk: 3.5/5 <br />The cover is okay. The girl is not exactly the way I picture Calla but it is still a pretty cover - enough to catch your attention. <br /><br />Final Thoughts: I am really enjoying this series and cannot wait to pick up Bloodrose!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5597098494038940114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14218886009944569770" style="display:none">TONS of info dumping and world building, which I hoped was over with in the first book. This love triangle might make me want to strangle myself. One thing that I don't love is how unattached to the characters the author seems to be. Good grief, a lot of important people die. It's almost as bad as James Dashner in his Maze Runner series. Just as I start to really like someone and feel like they are hugely important to the story, she kills them off. Meh. Just a personal preference, but I don't like that. I like rainbows and sunshine too much. Still, the storytelling is fantastic and I have NO IDEA how this series will end. I'm sort of team Ren, but I have a feeling that's not going to be how this plays out. Shay is too important to kill off or be second best :(<br /><br />(I'm listening to the audio of this series. <div id="review_160613465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160613465" />
    <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy"><img alt="All Things Urban Fantasy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320345194p2/2732683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160613465?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="All Things Urban Fantasy" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy">All Things Urban Fantasy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy?shelf=reviewed-by-abigail">reviewed-by-abigail</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160613465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer690923517686449267">Review courtesy of All Things Urban Fantasy<br/><br/>Call it the Sophomore slump, the second season syndrome, or what have you, but last year I gave NIGHTSHADE, the first book in the series of the same name by debut author Andrea Cremer, a perfect 5/5 rating. Today I’m giving the sequel, WOLFSBANE, a 2/5 rating. What happened to the story, the characters, the romance, and the writing between books one and two to cause such a drastic change? A lot of annoying, confusing, and boring things.<br/><br/>The mythology of </span>
  <span id="freeText690923517686449267" style="display:none">Review courtesy of All Things Urban Fantasy<br /><br />Call it the Sophomore slump, the second season syndrome, or what have you, but last year I gave NIGHTSHADE, the first book in the series of the same name by debut author Andrea Cremer, a perfect 5/5 rating. Today I’m giving the sequel, WOLFSBANE, a 2/5 rating. What happened to the story, the characters, the romance, and the writing between books one and two to cause such a drastic change? A lot of annoying, confusing, and boring things.<br /><br />The mythology of the Keepers, Guardians, Searchers, and the Scion still offer an interesting twist on witch, werewolf, and demon mythologies. Likewise the sociopolitical interactions of each group are well thought out and have wide reaching effects on themselves and each other. Andrea Cremer’s background as a history professor comes into play as well providing a detailed and very realistic origin for her mythologies. Unfortunately, those are about the only good things I can say about WOLFSBANE.<br /><br />Just about everything I loved about NIGHTSHADE is absent in WOLFSBANE. The forbidden love triangle between Calla, Shay and Ren? Not so forbidden anymore. But don’t tell Calla. She still anguishes over which guy to choose ad nauseam. Shay, barely recognizable in this sequel as a whiny possessive hot head, bears the brunt of her indecisiveness. Calla still wants to make out (and more) with Shay until mid smooch session when she’ll abruptly shove him away out of guilt over Ren. But then the situation just repeats a few chapters later.<br /><br />More annoying still was the plethora of new and extremely irritating characters. NIGHTSHADE was all about the wolves, WOLFSBANE is all about the Searchers. In the first few chapters a dozen new characters strut in and out of scenes with lots of desperate attempts at humor and inside jokes to show how close they all are. It was like a badly cast reality show. Calla and Shay basically just watch and ask zero questions about why they are there, what they are being asked to do, what the ultimate plan is, why they are so desperately needed etc. They are just ordered around and basically meekly obey. Well, Calla grows and shifts back and forth a lot, but that’s about it. <br /><br />90% of WOLFSBANE takes place in the Searchers academy and mostly consists of the Searchers inappropriately timed jokes (like after people just died), stupid sexual come ons, and lots and lots of history lessons. The last hundred pages or so finally spark with a bit of energy and action along with the first appearance of some of the original characters from NIGHTSHADE, but it wasn’t nearly enough to compensate for the rest of this extremely disappointing sequel. The third book in the Nightshade series is titled BLOODROSE and will be published on February 21, 2012. Based solely on the strength of the first book, I still plan to read it, but I’m keeping my expectations firmly in check.<br /><br />Sexual Content:<br />Heterosexual and homosexual kissing. Scenes of sensuality. A non graphic sex scene. References to rape. A scene that might have been an attempted sexual assault.</span>
  <a data-text-id="690923517686449267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3036074711253270927" style="display:none">I hope this cover is actually used. The other one is not something I want marring my shelf of lovely booklings. I take great pleasure in having splendid books, regardless of cover, but the other cover for this book is disturbing to me. <br /><br />Grr.<br /><br /><b>Update</b>: Yuck. Seriously, I loved <i>Nightshade</i>'s cover, so I bought the book and --in turn-- fell in love with the story. And then the publishers or whomever go and change the <i>Wolfsbane</i> cover. Wtheck? Is this not a YA fiction book? What's with the "Sexy cover"? Teens don't need any more "sexy" things. Seriously. Sex appeal isn't what should be selling a book. The story should. The writing. The characters. I MEAN REALLY? What was so wrong with the original covers?<br /><br /> And I don't buy that it was done to expand to the adult fiction audience. Whatever. I know zero adults who would buy the book with the new cover but not the old. Most people I know (including adults) would rather have the beautiful covers that were first advertised/used for the books. <br /><br /> They fit the story better, if you ask me. (And I don't care if you're not asking me.) They showed Calla in <i>nature</i>. They showed her as beautiful without having to resort to almost-innappropriate images.<br /><br /> I'm sixteen and if my mother saw this book in my hands she'd take it. I talked to her about it. The only way I'm allowed to buy <i>Wolfsbane</i> and know what happens next is if I get rid of the dustjacket. It's way beyond sad to know how downhill the world has gone.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_139051190" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139051190" />
    <a title="Dija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2857113-dija"><img alt="Dija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360335537p2/2857113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139051190?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dija" href="/user/show/2857113-dija">Dija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=authors-i-stalk">authors-i-stalk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139051190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12605290853709246154"><i>
  <blockquote>“What in life is worth a sacrifice, if not love?”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>After reading so many PNR adult novels, the first thing that always strikes me about YA novels is the smooth writing. I can't pinpoint what it is, exactly, that I love so much about it. Maybe it's just a lot more simpler to read or something, but I just love how the story flows off the page and each scene blends into the next without any pause or break in between. <br/><br/><i>Wolfsbane</i> picks up right where <i>Nightshade</i> left off. After helping Shay escape, C</span>
  <span id="freeText12605290853709246154" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“What in life is worth a sacrifice, if not love?”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>After reading so many PNR adult novels, the first thing that always strikes me about YA novels is the smooth writing. I can't pinpoint what it is, exactly, that I love so much about it. Maybe it's just a lot more simpler to read or something, but I just love how the story flows off the page and each scene blends into the next without any pause or break in between. <br><br><i>Wolfsbane</i> picks up right where <i>Nightshade</i> left off. After helping Shay escape, Calla finds herself in the midst of the Searchers, but instead of viewing them as the enemy, she starts to finally see through the lies the Keepers have fed her all her life, and decides to give all she's got to the Searcher's cause and her dream: freedom.<br><br>The consequences of Calla's actions are terrifying. I felt sick just reading about what the Keepers had done to her family and pack after her betrayal. And through it all, I couldn't help wishing Shay was dead so none of this would have happened. And I wish Calla hadn't been so shortsighted and gullible in running away with Shay, thinking that her actions would only have mild consequences, not anticipating all the tragedies that resulted from her foolish "love" for Shay. <br><br>But despite all that, I don't hate Calla, or even dislike her. She realizes that all the terror that has befallen her loved ones is her fault and after accepting it, she grows from it and becomes a stronger, better person. The selfish girl she was in <i>Nightshade</i> has developed into an admirable and responsible young woman in <i>Wolfsbane</i>, and I really love her for it. <br><br>I can't stand Shay. If anything, I hate him more in <i>Wolfsbane</i> than in <i>Nightshade</i>. He's immature, boring, selfish, and completely overbearing. At several points in the story, he gave me the rather unsettling impression of a rapist in the making. Calla pushed him away lots of times, and he kept on insisting and if Calla had been a weaker girl, I hate to see where it would have led. <br><br>Every time I read an argument between Calla and Shay, and there were A LOT of them in this book, I felt like doing a little jig around the room. <br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/jig/TheLadWhoLived/Jig.gif?o=0" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380343611ra/698944.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Why it's blatantly obvious to me that Calla is NOT in love with Shay:</b><br><br>1. She never runs to him for comfort, and rejects him when he offers it. <br>2. Every time she's reminded of Ren, and even times when she isn't, she turns away from him and pushes him away rather than talking it out. <br>3. She's reluctant about letting things progress farther than kissing between them. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And yes, I am ignoring the last 50-some pages of the book on purpose. She would have never let Shay get that close to her if Ren hadn't betrayed her. She was just hurting, and let Shay comfort her. That's all there was to it, and I'm not ready to accept otherwise, because then all the positive feelings I've been feeling for Calla would go down the drain. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>4. She can't stand it when he decides things for her, even though if she'd truly loved him, she would have been more understanding of his worry and concern.<br>5. She treats him like a subordinate, not like her equal. <br>6. She refuses to take off Ren's ring, even after Shay asks her to. <br>7. And lastly: SHE'S IN LOVE WITH REN!!!! I don't care how long it takes for her to admit it, but she's fangs over paws for Ren, and Shay is just a result of her teenage rebellious stage. She hates the power that the Keepers have over her, and in order to prove that she can run her life by herself, she takes off with Shay. <br><br>There's a completely new set of cast in <i>Wolfsbane</i> because now Calla's among the Searchers rather than the Keepers. The Searchers have a true bond between them similar to the bond among the Nightshades. I love how Silas, Ethan, Connor, and Adne are always teasing each other and making the best of their situation. Their firm resolve and the ability to always keep their eye on the future are qualities I find extremely remarkable and refreshing from Calla's occasional shortsightedness. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You haven’t had time to stumble across love yet.”<br>“Sure she has.” Connor slid into the chair on the other side of Adne, throwing his arm around her shoulders. “She just doesn’t appreciate it yet.”<br>Adne groaned and dropped her forehead onto the table. “I’ll marry the first person who gets me a cup of coffee, I don’t care who it is.”<br>“Throw me a mug, Isaac!” Connor half rose.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Connor and Adne are my new favorite duo in this series! I loved their constant bickering, silent support of one another, and the trust they have in each other's abilities. I hope there's a lot more of them, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[AnselxBryn, and SabinexEthan  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in <i>Bloodrose</i>.<br><br>I can't believe this series is ending in just one more book. I've really come to love these characters and I wish there's a spin-off featuring the side characters, or something. As for <i>Bloodrose</i>, I have only one <s>prayer</s> request: Please, please let Calla end up with Ren.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12605290853709246154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7psahvAnU3Qvi96PS4h+valNBx8dWQP6FjVYlf59YJnUvXNUS3maHIigau68fXRifxLg19PUjZ1NSx4kMz6SAw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<span id="freeTextContainer8895375448530043041">Andrea Cremer also known as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19642195.Andrea_Robertson' title='Andrea Robertson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Andrea Robertson</a>, is the author of the internationally bestselling Nightshade series. Before she wrote her first novel, A</span>
  <span id="freeText8895375448530043041" style="display:none">Andrea Cremer also known as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19642195.Andrea_Robertson" title="Andrea Robertson" rel="nofollow noopener">Andrea Robertson</a>, is the author of the internationally bestselling Nightshade series. She spent her childhood daydreaming and roaming the forests and lakeshores of Northern Wisconsin. <br /><br />Andrea has always loved writing and has never stopped writing, but she only recently plunged into the deep end of the pool that is professional writing. Before she wrote her first novel, Andrea was a history professor at Macalester College in St. Paul, Minnesota. In her books, she strives to bring together her two passions: history and fantasy. Andrea now lives in New York and writes full time.<br /><br />To contact Andrea, please visit, andreacremer.com <br /><br /><br /></span>
